## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form for (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Typical physics relationships combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v (often linear or nonlinear), and optional external/parametric time-dependent forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (pure Hooke-law restoring acceleration, no dissipation)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in normalized units)
- Constant-force bias / equilibrium shift: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (restoring dynamics around a shifted equilibrium)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (sliding friction modeled as constant-magnitude opposing acceleration)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (high-Re drag opposing motion)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with viscous damping)
- Duffing with harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator, resonance/chaos regimes)
- Pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (periodic restoring torque vs angle with damping)
- Parametric (Mathieu-type) stiffness modulation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance via time-varying stiffness)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - c2 * x**2) * v - c3 * x (self-excited oscillation with nonlinear damping leading to a limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 - c2 * x (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Liénard-type general form: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (state-dependent damping with linear restoring)
- Nonlinear restoring from potential expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3) - c3 * v (approximate conservative force via polynomial potential gradient)
- State-coupled stiffness/drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) - c3 * v * (c4 + c5 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness and damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring forces for symmetric oscillators are often odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(c*x)), which yields symmetric trajectories about x = 0.
- Linear damping appears as a term proportional to -v; additional -v*Abs(v) indicates drag whose magnitude grows faster with speed (typical of turbulent/aerodynamic regimes).
- A term like -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x indicates parametric excitation; instability tongues and parametric resonance occur when c2 is near twice the natural frequency.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior is suggested by damping that changes sign with state, e.g., (c0 - c1*x**2)*v or c0*v - c1*v**3 (energy injected at small amplitude, removed at large).
- Hardening/softening stiffness is indicated by an x**3 restoring term; it produces amplitude-dependent frequency and skewed resonance curves under forcing.
- Presence of cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) additive terms indicates external periodic forcing; combined with nonlinearity (x**3, sin(x)) can produce subharmonics and chaos.
- A sign(v) damping term suggests dry friction with stick–slip-like behavior and non-smooth dynamics near v = 0.
- If dv_dt can be written approximately as -dU/dx - c*v, then U(x) inferred from integrating the x-only part suggests conservative structure plus dissipation (useful for constraining symbolic forms).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO7)

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*x**c3

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(x,v)= -1.28311219603499\,x^3\;-\;0.0458938827292319\,v^3\;-\;0.729560991204844\,|v|^{1/3}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to **exactly** a linear combination of \(x^3\), \(v^3\), and \(|v|^{1/3}\) with **no extra dependence** on \(t\), no constants offsets, and no other \(x\) or \(v\) powers/functions.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all “extra” terms can be eliminated by setting their coefficients to 0 (or otherwise made identically 0), and then whether the remaining terms can match the three GT coefficients.

---

### 1. \(c0x^3+c1v^3+c2+c3|v|^{1/3}+c4\,v(c5+x)^{c6}\)
Set \(c2=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then it becomes \(c0x^3+c1v^3+c3|v|^{1/3}\), which can match GT by choosing:
- \(c0=-1.28311219603499\)
- \(c1=-0.0458938827292319\)
- \(c3=-0.729560991204844\)
So **matches**.

### 2. \(c0x^3+c1v^3+c2v+c3vx^2+c4+c5|v|^{1/3}\)

### 3. \(c0x^3+c1v^3+c2|v|^{1/3}+c3\,v(c4+x)^{c5}\)

### 63. \(c0x+c1x^3+c2v^3+c3+c4\log(c5|v|+1)+c6e^{c7x}|v|^{c8}\)
To match GT, must remove \(x\), constant, log, and exponential terms: set \(c0=0,c3=0,c4=0,c6=0\). Remaining \(c1x^3+c2v^3\) lacks \(|v|^{1/3}\) unless we keep the last term, but \(e^{c7x}|v|^{c8}\) cannot equal a pure \(|v|^{1/3}\) for all \(x\) unless \(c7=0\) (so \(e^{0}=1\)) and \(c8=1/3\). That would work, but only if we did **not** set \(c6=0\). So choose instead:
- \(c0=0,c3=0,c4=0\)
- \(c7=0,\;c8=1/3\)
Then expression becomes \(c1x^3+c2v^3+c6|v|^{1/3}\), which matches by setting \(c1,c2,c6\) to GT coefficients. **Matches**.
